< review>
As a person who is very critical of Arabic food, I can say without doubt that this is one of the best and most authentic middle eastern food places in San Diego. Often times restaurants claim to be middle eastern but they serve garbage. If you truly want to experience Lebanese home authentic cooking , this is the place to go. They put love into there food as is the Arab custom when feeding guests. On top of how amazing the food is, they are beyond reasonably priced. If you want a taste of home or just try authentic Arabic cuisine at its finest, then you have to try Karam‚Äôs !<//review>

Tiffany Williams< /username>
< Review>
The best part was the owner, who we got to know a little bit. He seems very nice, and the place seems very authentic. There were very cool decor, and had a nice homey atmosphere inside.

However, I'm unhappy to say that we did not get the stellar Mediterranean food that everyone has been raving about. Our beef shawarma was bland. The tahini was runny. There was a side of limp fries that look like they have been previously frozen and simply reheated, not seasoned. They could have done so much more with the fries (added feta, or some special sauce) but chose to make them as sad-looking as possible.

For the price that we paid, we were expecting higher quality in food.< /Review>

<Text>This place has a small cozy feel to it and the menu reflects that. You won't find a huge selection on their menu, but what they do have on their are all great choices. No matter what you choose whether the chicken shwarma, beef shwarma, a plate, a sandwich, or just some freshly made hummus and bread, they are all good choices.

The food is not too salty nor is it lacking in flavor. The meals hit the spot  and are made fairly quick. The drink selection is limited to bottled and canned drinks but if you came here for the food then that's hardly a gripe. I'm still waiting for them to add a breakfast menu, but in the meantime their delicious lunch menu can suffice for brunch.<//Text>< Resp>

< Text>
Outstanding service, good food, no air-conditioning, nice restroom, but toilet tank takes a long time to refill.  This is a very small place, with one table inside for more than 3 people, multiple tables for 2-3.  Couple more larger tables on the patio. We and our friends had a gyro wrap, chicken kabob, beef schawerma and chicken schawerma.  All were very good.  The schawermas were a bit dry, but had good char. Portions were good.  They charge $1.25 for sauces like tzaziki, garlic, spicy garlic, etc., but prices are pretty reasonable.  Salad had good quality greens. They supplied us with pitchers of ice water.  Lots of take-out business, and that's a good idea on a hot day.< /Text>

<username>raja kumar dash< /username><Rate>3</Rate>< Review>
I used to love Sprouts (would have given it 4/5 late last year), but lately it's been a waste of time going. For months and months back to fall 2018, neither the water section of their cooler nor the ready-to-eat food section is being maintained. And some of their clerks need training in common courtesy -- though this seems to be a problem at most stores in this area.

While I don't always drink cold bottled water, it's nice to have when the thirst strikes. Except no one is filling the shelves on a regular basis anymore. And today, they also shrunk the space in the cooler, adding more expensive, non-water drinks.

As for the food -- despite working at home, I sometimes need to grab a quick bite, and I usually incorporate that into other errands. Except my favorite, their once-delicious corn dog two-pack is almost never on the shelves anymore. Instead of my weekly (or sometimes twice-weekly) treat, It can be two months before I actually see any on the shelf, unlike last year.

To top off today with crazy, inconsiderate drivers in the parking lot, the clerk that served me couldn't be bothered to say hello, thank you, or goodbye, despite that I was polite and said those things. Like a lot of clerks around here, they ignore me but are polite to people served before and after me. My crime? I wish I knew.

Fortunately, Sprouts at this location still has frequent price drops for fresh fruit, and their packs/ bunches are always in good quality -- unlike other stores in the area with fruit rotting on the bottom of a pack/ bag.<//Review>

The set design was perfect for three reasons - it was was very straight forward with almost no excess clutter, you weren't misled by a gaggle of annoying red herrings, and it was perfectly medieval and totally immersive.  I felt like I an unwitting guest in the dining room of a demon-possessed, cannibalistic, medieval lord.

Once you've done as many rooms as I have, it's not often you get in that heart-racing panic to get out, but this room thrilled me, stressed me out, and delighted me in all the best ways possible.  The puzzles weren't frustrating or terribly hard, but the stress factor can make your mind go blank.  We asked for two hints - one in the very beginning which we definitely needed and one towards the end - and escaped with less than 2 minutes, so if you get stuck, don't sit there. Ask for help!  The game master wants you to get out, too!

Lord Garrick, Lord Garrick, Lord Garrick - if it weren't for the pandemic, I would have hugged both the actor and the game master when it was over for making this experience so fantastic.  He was so intimidating, and while his voice was deeply melodious, authoritative and lordly, his persona was subtly menacing and you knew at any moment that he would snap.

This is a room you can go to multiple times because the second time around, they will let you be part of the game while your friends suffer through it.  I absolutely plan on going back!  Well done, Quest Tavern!!<//text>< Pictures>

<Name>Gerardo Paz</Name><date>1583349634706<//date><response>None</response><Rate>5<//Rate><GmapID>0x80c32ff293921fa5:0xf846baec7449a04b<//GmapID><pictures>None<//pictures>< Text>
If I can give this place 6 stars I would.

Going through my reviews you'll notice that my fiance and I have done over 50 rooms. After going through The Witch's Cauldron and meeting with the owner we knew that we had to do Last Supper as that room was making waves in the ER community.

Witch's Cauldron is a very scrappy room with a strong atmosphere and great lighting. There are things that will stick out such as a digital clock and modern combination locks that clash with the old-time fantasy setting but we found them more charming than deal breakers. We had time to nerd out with the owner who is really chill. It was Witch's Cauldron charm and the owner's infectious enthusiasm that motivated my fiancee to not only book Last Supper but to book it as our 50 room milestone.

As for Last Supper, boy oh boy talk about improvement!

If Witch's Cauldron was the fun scrappy room then Last Super is the super-polished final output. That room was an utter BLAST to play filled with tension, fun puzzles and horror-comedy. This goes without saying that our actor was amazing with his strong performance anchoring the experience and really elevating the feeling of urgency. Also worth pointing out the adaptive soundtrack which stayed at a lull during slower moments only to ratchet up when stuff hit the fa really giving the room a full story arch. Get some friends and get over here to play BOTH their games.< /Text>

< Text>
My team recently completed "The Witch's Cauldron" at Quest Tavern.

With no hints, I would describe the difficulty of this room as firmly 'intermediate.' However this room has the impressive distinction of being very well put together AND having wonderful game masters.
That means that players of all skill levels will enjoy the experience equally, as the game masters - if needed - seem to know exactly how to nudge you in the right direction without giving too much away.

All that combines with clever puzzles, strong aesthetic design, and a seamless flow to give an experience that is well worth the time and money.

I recommend this room for everyone, and I will be back to try more of Quest Tavern's rooms as soon as they are available.<//Text>

<rating>5<//rating>< review>
I had the pleasure of playing both of their AH-MAZING rooms last night.
First off, their lobby/entrance area is spacious, welcoming and beautifully themed. It really sets the theme for the rooms you‚Äôre about to experience. From their sign in, to little mini games while you wait, it‚Äôs all in the details. They even have a ‚ÄúQuest board‚Äù like in role playing games/adventures is where you would go to accept quests.
Now let‚Äôs talk about their rooms:
- The Witches Cauldron: this is the less scary of the two so if you aren‚Äôt a fan of scary or scare actors, I would recommend this room. The immersement begins before you even enter the room. From the get-go with the story, you are continuously immersed in the room and the story. The puzzles match the theme really well. There‚Äôs a nice level of difficulty to challenge those who like to be challenged. For those who need a little nudge, there‚Äôs a way to ask for guidance if needed.
I thoroughly enjoyed this room for its puzzles, theme, immersement and layout.
- The Last Supper: this is the scarier of the two and includes a live scare actor. So if you aren‚Äôt up for this, maybe stick with the Witches Cauldron. Otherwise, I highly recommend The Last Supper.
The beautiful thing about this is that you have to interact with the live scare actor. I‚Äôve never had that before so it made for a new kind of experience and I loved it. It really makes you think on your feet, adds the element of fear and nervousness and really adds to the overall challenge. The rooms puzzles  were again nicely themed, a good amount of difficulty and included a variety so they didn‚Äôt seem repetitive. The live scare actor was absolutely brilliant! I couldn‚Äôt recommend him enough and apparently he‚Äôs the ‚Äúscariest‚Äù of them so I‚Äôm glad we got the full experience for our game.
The team at Quest Tavern are all wonderful people. Very friendly, they enjoy a good laugh, super accommodating and they play their roles extremely well. Definitely the best Escape Room I‚Äôve done so far in my Escape Room adventures.
Do it - you won‚Äôt regret it :)< /review>

We've been using eSign Genie, often daily, for a few months now, after changing from another comparably-priced software that we used for a year.  eSign Genie has proven more straight-forward for both ourselves and our signers. <Date>1595037958108< /Date>< Rate>

< text>
Share review

Embed review

7/17/2020
These are my recollections and impressions of purchasing a used vehicle from YC Honda.

I signed papers gir a vehicle, a 2011 GMC Terrain, on the 12th, and agreed I would pick it up four days later.

I was asked to email my salesman proof of income. I did on the 13th. On the 14th, Dennis in finance said I had to bring in proof of income because he didn't have them. Obviously my salesman never forwarded the documents to the finance staff. Then after I emailed them to Dennis, he says I have to come in and re-sign a document because another finance staffer had previously erred on one document. Finally,  Thursday arrives.

The salesman picks me up st home, and we get to the dealership. Had to wait because the SUV was dirty. Apparently, the dealership had an issue with its detail staff. Mind you there's a car wash almost across the street and the dealership had three days to get the vehicle clean. The salesman hosed off the exterior with what he called soft water so, he explained,  it wouldn't leave spots. It left spots in spite of that. The salesman did not clean the inside of the windshield which was filthy.

The salesman and I had agreed that he would connect the Blue Tooth to my phone. He was unable to do it, explaining that I had to have On-Star to have Blue Tooth. Subsequently I learned from a GMC dealer that the vehicle doesn't have Blue Tooth, and that, even if it did,  that I would not need On-Star. You would think that people would do some research on vehicles they sell, but they don't at YC Honda.

Anyway, the salesman said he would call me later that afternoon about getting the Blue Tooth connected.  Never heard from him since.

Before he left, the salesman gave me a second key fob which was badly broken. I insisted on a fully functional key fob,  and had to come back later to get one. Several days later, one of the managers told me that I was not entitled to two key fobs and he wouldn't have given me a replacement.

My salesman said that the oil and filter were recently changed, but the truck's electronics indicated the oil was at 71% of its life expectancy. Now I've never heard of new oil losing 29% of its life in a short period of time.

Doubting that their alleged master mechanic had checked out my SUV, I took it to another dealer who found several issues including a reverse light which was out (a safety issue), grossly misaligned rear wheels, over inflated tires (35 to 40 PSI, not the 32 PSI recommended). I had that dealer makes all necessary adjustments,  and took the car to a car wash to get the SUV cleaned add ir should have been.

I spent over $176 to bring the vehicle to where it should have been. A Honda manager said I should have returned the SUV to Honda. I asked why since they couldn't check out the SUV in the days before I picked it up.

They also failed to tell me that the cargo cover was missing, and that it was no longer available. That would have indicated some level of integrity,  but no - not from YC Honda.

I will never buy a vehicle from YC Honda again.</text>

They even sent me a courtesy email letting me know that there were two open recalls on my CR-V (which I verified via Honda's corporate website).  I opted to go back for the high-mileage preventative maintenance and rear breaks.  Personnel were attentive, and even washed my car before I left.  They also post useful coupons on their website, which saved me 15% off my bill.

<rating>5< /rating><Review>This wonderful store is a block from our home; another grocery store is also within an easy stroll from our place, but 9 times out of 10 we shop at Grocery Outlet.  Grocery Outlet is far more affordable, the staff is friendly and efficient, and they greet regular customers by name. Most items are ‚Äòbrand name‚Äô and perfect quality. You might have to check expiration dates on perishable items, but rarely do I find anything close to, or out of date.

Shopping here is a bit of ‚Äòhit or miss‚Äô. You can‚Äôt go in with a shopping list and expect every item to be available. Peanut butter? Yes, but not necessarily your preferred brand. Tea bags? Usually not. But, somethings are always available, at low prices, with great selections: olive oils, wine (some real deals here if you‚Äôre familiar with the selections on the shelf) and an amazing array of table cheeses.

We typically buy fruit, vegetables, dairy products, and other staples here. Admittedly, when we do buy meat or poultry we go to the food coop or farmers‚Äô market. If we need a particular item, maybe vanilla extract, or baking soda, or a spice that‚Äôs a bit uncommon, etc. we head to a bigger (triple the price) grocery store. But, overall, we much prefer Grocery Outlet.</Review>< pictures>

<Rate>4<//Rate>< Text>
The first Grocery Outlet that I went to was in Monterey when I was on a trip with my lovely group of Girl Scouts. Amazed by the prices and an overall decent selection, I decided to find the nearest one to me. Granted this is not it, but it is very convenient to my uni. I like this location because it is simple to locate (right off of L street) and is one of the newer stores in Sacramento. Like earlier reviewers have said, it has a grande selection of every cheese imaginable and if I were thinking at the time, I would have picked at least two to have an awesome and simple dish of macaroni pasta. I must say that they have a good selection of wine and beer! I liked the easy layout of this particular Grocery Outlet, but it is on the small side. I would only come back here again to pick up something for a meal later on in that day or for some of their cheeses. There really isn't much to this store.<//Text>

<pics>None< /pics>< Text>
Very affordable location. They may not have everything you're looking for, but as a supplemental place you can get staples and deals on overstock items, and the owners of this location are in touch with the community. The first aisle often has pretty good deals on non-grocery items like holiday stuff, makeup extras, salon/hair products, protein/dieting products. Small fruit/veggie section. Lots of processed food aisles. Workers are laid back and helpful. Parking is easy. Beware the pushcarts if you park on the street, because I got embarrassed when suddenly my pushcart when over an invisible line and the wheelblockers were activated and I thought i ran over a rock or something, until somebody told me "hey! you cannot push the carts to the street, they boot the wheels!" Ohhhhh.<//Text>

<UserId.>101045205518069290501<//UserId.><Time>1479676036030< /Time>< review>
I can't say this is a typical grocery outlet store, but I enjoy shopping here for good bargains and what nots. I typically go down every aisle to find things I need and others I didnt know I needed. The produce here always looks fresh and it's a pretty clean store also. And if you love wine, they have a selection that could rival Trader Joe's in volume and price. Overall, a good place that could either be your go-to store, or a store that has weekly bargains as the inventory continues to rotate based upon the popularity of the selection. Glad they're here.<//review>
